href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Year_of_established.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="344" data-file-width="792" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Virginia-Year_of_established.svg/200px-Virginia-Year_of_established.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Virginia-Year_of_established.svg/300px-Virginia-Year_of_established.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Virginia-Year_of_established.svg/400px-Virginia-Year_of_established.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virginia-Year_of_established.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nVirginia counties and cities by year of establishment</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Commonwealth of Virginia</a> is divided into 95 counties, along with 38 <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">independent cities</a> that are considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County-equivalent" title="County-equivalent">county-equivalents</a> for census purposes. The map in this article, taken from the official <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> site, includes <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Forge,_Virginia" title="Clifton Forge, Virginia">Clifton Forge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bedford,_Virginia" title="Bedford, Virginia">Bedford</a> as independent cities. This reflected the political reality at the time of the 2000 Census. However, both have since chosen to revert to town status. In Virginia, cities are co-equal levels of government to counties, but towns are part of counties. For some counties, for statistical purposes, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a> combines any independent cities with the county that it was once part of (before the legislation creating independent cities took place in 1871).</p>\n<p>Many county seats are politically not a part of the counties they serve; under Virginia law, all municipalities incorporated as cities are <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">independent cities</a> and are not part of any county. Some of the cities in the <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> area (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach" title="Virginia Beach">Virginia Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">Chesapeake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">Newport News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">Hampton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">Suffolk</a>) were formed from an entire county. These cities are no longer county seats, since the counties ceased to exist once the cities were completely formed, but are functionally equivalent to counties.</p>\n<p>There are several counties and cities which have the same name, but are separate politically. These currently include Fairfax, Franklin, Richmond, and Roanoke. In the past they also included Norfolk and Alexandria, whose counties changed their names, ostensibly to end some of the confusion; as well as Bedford, where a city was surrounded by a county of the same name from 1968 until 2013, when the city reverted to town status. A city and county that share a name may be completely unrelated in geography. For example, Richmond County is nowhere near the City of Richmond, and Franklin County is even farther from the City of Franklin.</p>\n<p>More Virginia counties are named for women than in any other state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Virginia\'s postal abbreviation is <b>VA</b> and its FIPS state code is <b>51</b>.</p>\n<p>List of the 95 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> (links shown under <b>FIPS County Code</b> are for the U.S. Census Bureau Statistics Info Page for that county):</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" rel="nofollow">001</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Accomac,_Virginia" title="Accomac, Virginia">Accomac</a></td>\n<td>1663</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Accomac_Shire" title="Accomac Shire">Accomac Shire</a> was established in 1634 as one of the original eight <a href="/wiki/Shires_of_Virginia" title="Shires of Virginia">shires of Virginia</a>. In 1642, it was renamed Northampton County. Then in 1663, Northampton County was divided into two counties. The southern half remained Northampton County while the northern half became Accomac County -- later renamed Accomack with a "k.".</td>\n<td>From the Native American word Accawmack, meaning "on the Virginia">Fincastle</a> (1772\xe2\x80\x931776), formed from territory claimed by <a href="/wiki/Botetourt_County,_Virginia" title="Botetourt County, Virginia">Botetourt Co.</a> &amp; including western Virginia</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kentucky_County,_Virginia" title="Kentucky County, Virginia">Kentucky</a> (1776\xe2\x80\x931780), formed from Fincastle\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fayette_County,_Kentucky" title="Fayette County, Kentucky">Fayette</a> (1780\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Kentucky Co., centered on <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Kentucky" title="Lexington, Kentucky">Lexington</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>\n<ul>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourbon_County,_Virginia" title="Bourbon County, Virginia">Bourbon</a> (1785\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Fayette, centered on <a href="/wiki/Paris,_Kentucky" title="Paris, Kentucky">Paris</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>\n<ul>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_counties,_cities,_and_towns_of_Virginia" title="Former counties, cities, and towns of Virginia">Mason</a> (1788\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Bourbon, centered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limestone,_Kentucky" title="Limestone, Kentucky">Limestone</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodford_County,_Virginia" title="Woodford County, Virginia">Woodford</a> (1788\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Fayette, centered on <a href="/wiki/Versailles,_Kentucky" title="Versailles, Kentucky">Versailles</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Kentucky" title="Jefferson County, Kentucky">Jefferson</a> (1780\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Kentucky Co., href="/wiki/Nelson_County,_Virginia" title="Nelson County, Virginia">Nelson</a> (1782\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Jefferson, centered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baird%27s_Town,_Kentucky" href="/wiki/Lincoln_County,_Virginia" title="Lincoln County, Virginia">Lincoln</a> (1780\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Kentucky Co., centered first on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harrodstown,_Kentucky" title="Harrodstown, Kentucky">Harrodstown</a> then on <a href="/wiki/Stanford,_Kentucky" title="Stanford, Kentucky">Stanford</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Madison_County,_Virginia" title="Madison County, Virginia">Madison</a> (1785\xe2\x80\x931792), formed from Lincoln, centered on <a href="/wiki/Milford,_Kentucky" title="Milford, Kentucky">Milford</a>, and seceded to form <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Virginia">West Virginia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
